class="mw-body" role="main">\n\t\t\t<a id="top"></a>\n\t\t\t<div id="siteNotice" class="mw-body-content"><!-- CentralNotice --></div><div class="mw-indicators mw-body-content">\n<div id="mw-indicator-pp-default" class="mw-indicator"><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Protection_policy#semi" title="This article is semi-protected due to vandalism"><img alt="Page semi-protected" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fc/Padlock-silver.svg/20px-Padlock-silver.svg.png" width="20" height="20" //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fc/Padlock-silver.svg/40px-Padlock-silver.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="128" data-file-height="128" /></a></div>\n</div>\n<h1 id="firstHeading" class="firstHeading" lang="en">Helicopter</h1>\t\t\t<div id="bodyContent" class="mw-body-content">\n\t\t\t\t<div id="siteSub" class="noprint">From Wikipedia, the free encyclopedia</div>\t\t\t\t<div id="contentSub"></div>\n\t\t\t\t<div id="jump-to-nav"></div>\t\t\t\t<a class="mw-jump-link" href="#mw-head">Jump to navigation</a>\n\t\t\t\t<a class="mw-jump-link" href="#p-search">Jump to search</a>\n\t\t\t\t<div id="mw-content-text" lang="en" dir="ltr" class="mw-content-ltr"><div class="mw-parser-output"><div class="shortdescription nomobile noexcerpt noprint searchaux" style="display:none">Type of rotor craft in which lift and thrust are supplied by rotors</div>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">"Helicopters" redirects here. For other uses, see <a href="/wiki/Helicopter_(disambiguation)" class="mw-disambig" title="Helicopter (disambiguation)">Helicopter (disambiguation)</a>.</div>\n<p class="mw-empty-elt">\n\n\n</p>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:LAPD_Bell_206_Jetranger.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/78/LAPD_Bell_206_Jetranger.jpg/220px-LAPD_Bell_206_Jetranger.jpg" width="220" height="147" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/78/LAPD_Bell_206_Jetranger.jpg/330px-LAPD_Bell_206_Jetranger.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/78/LAPD_Bell_206_Jetranger.jpg/440px-LAPD_Bell_206_Jetranger.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2856" data-file-height="1904" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:LAPD_Bell_206_Jetranger.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>A <a href="/wiki/Bell_206" title="Bell 206">Bell 206</a> helicopter of the <a href="/wiki/Los_Angeles_Police_Department" title="Los Angeles Police Department">Los Angeles Police Department</a></div></div></div>\n<p>A <b>helicopter</b> is a type of <a href="/wiki/Rotorcraft" title="Rotorcraft">rotorcraft</a> in which <a href="/wiki/Lift_(force)" title="Lift (force)">lift</a> and <a href="/wiki/Thrust" title="Thrust">thrust</a> are supplied by <a href="/wiki/Helicopter_rotor" title="Helicopter rotor">rotors</a>.  This allows the helicopter to take off and land vertically, to <a href="/wiki/Hover_(helicopter)" class="mw-redirect" title="Hover (helicopter)">hover</a>, and to fly forward, backward, and laterally. These attributes allow helicopters to be used in congested or isolated areas where <a href="/wiki/Fixed-wing_aircraft" title="Fixed-wing aircraft">fixed-wing aircraft</a> and many forms of <a href="/wiki/VTOL" title="VTOL">VTOL</a> (vertical takeoff and landing) aircraft cannot perform.\n</p><p>The English word <i>helicopter</i> is adapted from the French word <i lang="fr" title="French language text">h\xc3\xa9licopt\xc3\xa8re</i>, coined by <a href="/w/index.php?title=Gustave_Ponton_d%27Am%C3%A9court&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Gustave Ponton d&#39;Am\xc3\xa9court (page does not exist)">Gustave Ponton d\'Am\xc3\xa9court</a> in 1861, which originates from the <a href="/wiki/Greek_language" title="Greek language">Greek</a> <i>helix</i> (<span lang="grc" title="Ancient Greek language text">\xe1\xbc\x95\xce\xbb\xce\xb9\xce\xbe</span>) "helix, spiral, whirl, convolution"<sup id="cite_ref-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-1">&#91;1&#93;</a></sup> and <i>pteron</i> (<span lang="grc" title="Ancient Greek language text">\xcf\x80\xcf\x84\xce\xb5\xcf\x81\xcf\x8c\xce\xbd</span>) "wing".<sup id="cite_ref-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-2">&#91;2&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-3">&#91;3&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-4">&#91;4&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-5" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-5">&#91;5&#93;</a></sup> English language nicknames for helicopter include "chopper", "copter", "helo", "heli", and "whirlybird".\n</p><p>Helicopters were developed and built during the first half-century of <a href="/wiki/Flight" title="Flight">flight</a>, with the <a href="/wiki/Focke-Wulf_Fw_61" title="Focke-Wulf Fw 61">Focke-Wulf Fw 61</a> being the first operational helicopter in 1936.  Some helicopters reached limited production, but it was not until 1942 that a helicopter designed by <a href="/wiki/Igor_Sikorsky" title="Igor Sikorsky">Igor Sikorsky</a> reached full-scale <a href="/wiki/Mass_production" title="Mass production">production</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-Munson_6-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Munson-6">&#91;6&#93;</a></sup> with 131 aircraft built.<sup id="cite_ref-Hirschberg_7-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Hirschberg-7">&#91;7&#93;</a></sup>  Though most earlier designs used more than one main rotor, it is the single main rotor with anti-torque <a href="/wiki/Tail_rotor" title="Tail rotor">tail rotor</a> configuration that has become the most common helicopter configuration.  <a href="/wiki/Tandem_rotor" class="mw-redirect" title="Tandem rotor">Tandem rotor</a> helicopters are also in widespread use due to their greater payload capacity.  <a href="/wiki/Coaxial_rotors" title="Coaxial rotors">Coaxial</a> helicopters, <a href="/wiki/Tiltrotor" title="Tiltrotor">tiltrotor</a> aircraft, and <a href="/wiki/Gyrodyne" title="Gyrodyne">compound helicopters</a> are all flying today.  <a href="/wiki/Quadcopter" title="Quadcopter">Quadcopter</a> helicopters pioneered as <a href="/wiki/Breguet-Richet_Gyroplane" title="Breguet-Richet Gyroplane">early as 1907</a> in France, and other types of <a href="/wiki/Multicopter" class="mw-redirect" title="Multicopter">multicopter</a> have been developed for specialized applications such as unmanned drones.\n</p>\n<div id="toc" class="toc"><input type="checkbox" role="button" id="toctogglecheckbox" class="toctogglecheckbox" style="display:none" /><div class="toctitle" lang="en" dir="ltr"><h2>Contents</h2><span class="toctogglespan"><label links</span></a></li>\n</ul>\n</div>\n\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="History">History</span></h2>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Early_design">Early design</span></h3>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">See also: <a href="/wiki/Bamboo-copter" title="Bamboo-copter">Bamboo-copter</a> and <a href="/wiki/Science_and_inventions_of_Leonardo_da_Vinci" title="Science and inventions of Leonardo da Vinci">Science and inventions of Leonardo da Vinci</a></div>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Taketombo.JPG" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/54/Taketombo.JPG/220px-Taketombo.JPG" width="220" height="159" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/54/Taketombo.JPG/330px-Taketombo.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/54/Taketombo.JPG/440px-Taketombo.JPG 2x" data-file-width="1287" data-file-height="933" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Taketombo.JPG" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>A decorated Japanese <i>taketombo</i> bamboo-copter</div></div></div>\n<p>The earliest references for vertical flight came from China. Since around 400 BC,<sup id="cite_ref-Gordon_8-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Gordon-8">&#91;8&#93;</a></sup> Chinese children have played with <a href="/wiki/Bamboo-copter" title="Bamboo-copter">bamboo flying toys</a> (or Chinese top).<sup id="cite_ref-9" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-9">&#91;9&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Taking_Flight:_Inventing_the_Aerial_Age,_from_Antiquity_Through_the_First_World_War_10-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Taking_Flight:_Inventing_the_Aerial_Age,_from_Antiquity_Through_the_First_World_War-10">&#91;10&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-china-1_11-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-china-1-11">&#91;11&#93;</a></sup> This bamboo-copter is spun by rolling a stick attached to a rotor. The spinning creates lift, and the toy flies when released.<sup id="cite_ref-Gordon_8-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Gordon-8">&#91;8&#93;</a></sup> The 4th-century AD <a href="/wiki/Daoist" class="mw-redirect" title="Daoist">Daoist</a> book <i><a href="/wiki/Baopuzi" title="Baopuzi">Baopuzi</a></i> by <a href="/wiki/Ge_Hong" title="Ge Hong">Ge Hong</a> (<span lang="ch">\xe6\x8a\xb1\xe6\x9c\xb4\xe5\xad\x90 "Master who Embraces Simplicity") reportedly describes some of the ideas inherent to rotary wing aircraft.<sup id="cite_ref-china-2_12-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-china-2-12">&#91;12&#93;</a></sup>\n</span></p><p>Designs similar to the Chinese helicopter toy appeared in some Renaissance paintings and other works.<sup id="cite_ref-13" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-13">&#91;13&#93;</a></sup>  In the 18th and early 19th centuries Western scientists developed flying machines based on the Chinese toy.<sup id="cite_ref-Leishman_2006,_p._8_14-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Leishman_2006,_p._8-14">&#91;14&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Leonardo_da_Vinci_helicopter.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/37/Leonardo_da_Vinci_helicopter.jpg/220px-Leonardo_da_Vinci_helicopter.jpg" width="220" height="162" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/37/Leonardo_da_Vinci_helicopter.jpg/330px-Leonardo_da_Vinci_helicopter.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/3/37/Leonardo_da_Vinci_helicopter.jpg 2x" data-file-width="363" data-file-height="268" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Leonardo_da_Vinci_helicopter.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Leonardo\'s "aerial screw"</div></div></div>\n<p>It was not until the early 1480s, when Italian polymath <a href="/wiki/Leonardo_da_Vinci" title="Leonardo da Vinci">Leonardo da Vinci</a> created a design for a machine that could be described as an "aerial screw", that any recorded advancement was made towards vertical flight. His notes suggested that he built small flying models, but there were no indications for any provision to stop the rotor from making the craft rotate.<sup id="cite_ref-flight-1_15-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-flight-1-15">&#91;15&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-aerial_screw_16-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-aerial_screw-16">&#91;16&#93;</a></sup> As scientific knowledge increased and became more accepted, people continued to pursue the idea of vertical flight.\n</p>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Elicottero_sperimentale_Enrico_Forlanini_1877_Museo_scienza_e_tecnologia_Milano.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d7/Elicottero_sperimentale_Enrico_Forlanini_1877_Museo_scienza_e_tecnologia_Milano.jpg/220px-Elicottero_sperimentale_Enrico_Forlanini_1877_Museo_scienza_e_tecnologia_Milano.jpg" width="220" height="147" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d7/Elicottero_sperimentale_Enrico_Forlanini_1877_Museo_scienza_e_tecnologia_Milano.jpg/330px-Elicottero_sperimentale_Enrico_Forlanini_1877_Museo_scienza_e_tecnologia_Milano.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d7/Elicottero_sperimentale_Enrico_Forlanini_1877_Museo_scienza_e_tecnologia_Milano.jpg/440px-Elicottero_sperimentale_Enrico_Forlanini_1877_Museo_scienza_e_tecnologia_Milano.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2000" data-file-height="1333" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Elicottero_sperimentale_Enrico_Forlanini_1877_Museo_scienza_e_tecnologia_Milano.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Experimental helicopter by <a href="/wiki/Enrico_Forlanini" title="Enrico Forlanini">Enrico Forlanini</a>, 1877</div></div></div>\n<p>In July 1754, Russian <a href="/wiki/Mikhail_Lomonosov" title="Mikhail Lomonosov">Mikhail Lomonosov</a> had developed a small coaxial modeled after the Chinese top but powered by a wound-up spring device<sup id="cite_ref-Leishman_2006,_p._8_14-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Leishman_2006,_p._8-14">&#91;14&#93;</a></sup> and demonstrated it to the <a href="/wiki/Russian_Academy_of_Sciences" title="Russian Academy of Sciences">Russian Academy of Sciences</a>. It was powered by a spring, and was suggested as a method to lift <a href="/wiki/Meteorological" class="mw-redirect" title="Meteorological">meteorological</a> instruments. In 1783, <a href="/w/index.php?title=Christian_de_Launoy&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Christian de Launoy (page does not exist)">Christian de Launoy</a>, and his <a href="/wiki/Mechanic" title="Mechanic">mechanic</a>, Bienvenu, used a coaxial version of the Chinese top in a model consisting of contrarotating <a href="/wiki/Turkey_(bird)" title="Turkey (bird)">turkey</a> flight feathers<sup id="cite_ref-Leishman_2006,_p._8_14-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Leishman_2006,_p._8-14">&#91;14&#93;</a></sup> as rotor blades, and in 1784, demonstrated it to the <a href="/wiki/French_Academy_of_Sciences" title="French Academy of Sciences">French Academy of Sciences</a>. <a href="/wiki/Sir_George_Cayley" class="mw-redirect" title="Sir George Cayley">Sir George Cayley</a>, influenced by a childhood fascination with the Chinese flying top, developed a model of feathers, similar to that of Launoy and Bienvenu, but powered by rubber bands. By the end of the century, he had progressed to using sheets of tin for rotor blades and springs for power. His writings on his experiments and models would become influential on future aviation pioneers.<sup id="cite_ref-flight-1_15-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-flight-1-15">&#91;15&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Alphonse_P%C3%A9naud" title="Alphonse P\xc3\xa9naud">Alphonse P\xc3\xa9naud</a> would later develop coaxial rotor model helicopter toys in 1870, also powered by rubber bands. One of these toys, given as a gift by their father, would inspire the <a href="/wiki/Wright_brothers" title="Wright brothers">Wright brothers</a> to pursue the dream of flight.<sup id="cite_ref-17" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-17">&#91;17&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Lomonocov_s_Aerodynamic_Machine_01.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/ff/Lomonocov_s_Aerodynamic_Machine_01.jpg/170px-Lomonocov_s_Aerodynamic_Machine_01.jpg" width="170" height="230" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/ff/Lomonocov_s_Aerodynamic_Machine_01.jpg/255px-Lomonocov_s_Aerodynamic_Machine_01.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/ff/Lomonocov_s_Aerodynamic_Machine_01.jpg/340px-Lomonocov_s_Aerodynamic_Machine_01.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1547" data-file-height="2091" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Lomonocov_s_Aerodynamic_Machine_01.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Prototype created by <a href="/wiki/Mikhail_Lomonosov" title="Mikhail Lomonosov">M. Lomonosov</a>, 1754</div></div></div>\n<p>In 1861, the word "helicopter" was coined by <a href="/w/index.php?title=Gustave_de_Ponton_d%27Am%C3%A9court&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Gustave de Ponton d&#39;Am\xc3\xa9court (page does not exist)">Gustave de Ponton d\'Am\xc3\xa9court</a>, a French inventor who demonstrated a small steam-powered model. While celebrated as an innovative use of a new metal, aluminum, the model never lifted off the ground. D\'Amecourt\'s linguistic contribution would survive to eventually describe the vertical flight he had envisioned. Steam power was popular with other inventors as well. In 1878 the Italian <a href="/wiki/Enrico_Forlanini" title="Enrico Forlanini">Enrico Forlanini</a>\'s unmanned vehicle, also powered by a steam engine, rose to a height of 12 meters (40&#160;ft), where it hovered for some 20 seconds after a vertical take-off. Emmanuel Dieuaide\'s steam-powered design featured counter-rotating rotors powered through a hose from a boiler on the ground.<sup id="cite_ref-flight-1_15-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-flight-1-15">&#91;15&#93;</a></sup> In 1887 Parisian inventor, <a href="/wiki/Gustave_Trouv%C3%A9" title="Gustave Trouv\xc3\xa9">Gustave Trouv\xc3\xa9</a>, built and flew a tethered electric model helicopter.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (May 2015)">citation needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup>\n</p><p>In July 1901, the maiden flight of <a href="/wiki/Hermann_Ganswindt" title="Hermann Ganswindt">Hermann Ganswindt</a>\'s helicopter took place in Berlin-Sch\xc3\xb6neberg; this was probably the first motor-driven flight carrying humans. A movie covering the event was taken by <a href="/wiki/Max_Skladanowsky" title="Max Skladanowsky">Max Skladanowsky</a>, but it remains <a href="/wiki/Lost_film" title="Lost film">lost</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-18" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-18">&#91;18&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:US970616-Figure_1.png" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/89/US970616-Figure_1.png/220px-US970616-Figure_1.png" width="220" height="130" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/89/US970616-Figure_1.png/330px-US970616-Figure_1.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/89/US970616-Figure_1.png/440px-US970616-Figure_1.png 2x" data-file-width="1988" data-file-height="1172" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:US970616-Figure_1.png" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Drawing from Edison\'s 1910 patent<sup id="cite_ref-us970616_19-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-us970616-19">&#91;19&#93;</a></sup></div></div></div>\n<p>In 1885, <a href="/wiki/Thomas_Edison" title="Thomas Edison">Thomas Edison</a> was given US$1,000 by <a href="/wiki/James_Gordon_Bennett,_Jr." class="mw-redirect" title="James Gordon Bennett, Jr.">James Gordon Bennett, Jr.</a>, to conduct experiments towards developing flight. Edison built a helicopter and used the paper for a stock ticker to create <a href="/wiki/Guncotton" class="mw-redirect" title="Guncotton">guncotton</a>, with which he attempted to power an internal combustion engine. The helicopter was damaged by explosions and one of his workers was badly burned. Edison reported that it would take a motor with a ratio of three to four pounds per horsepower produced to be successful, based on his experiments.<sup id="cite_ref-20" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-20">&#91;20&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/J%C3%A1n_Bah%C3%BD%C4%BE" title="J\xc3\xa1n Bah\xc3\xbd\xc4\xbe">J\xc3\xa1n Bah\xc3\xbd\xc4\xbe</a>, a <a href="/wiki/Slovaks" title="Slovaks">Slovak</a> inventor, adapted the <a href="/wiki/Internal_combustion_engine" title="Internal combustion engine">internal combustion engine</a> to power his helicopter model that reached a height of 0.5 meters (1.6&#160;ft) in 1901. On 5 May 1905, his helicopter reached four meters (13&#160;ft) in altitude and flew for over 1,500 meters (4,900&#160;ft).<sup id="cite_ref-21" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-21">&#91;21&#93;</a></sup> In 1908, Edison patented his own design for a helicopter powered by a gasoline engine with box kites attached to a mast by cables for a rotor,<sup id="cite_ref-us970616_19-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-us970616-19">&#91;19&#93;</a></sup> but it never flew.<sup id="cite_ref-22" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-22">&#91;22&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="First_flights">First flights</span></h3>\n<p>In 1906, two French brothers, Jacques and <a href="/wiki/Louis_Breguet" class="mw-redirect" title="Louis Breguet">Louis Breguet</a>, began experimenting with airfoils for helicopters. In 1907, those experiments resulted in the <a href="/wiki/Breguet-Richet_Gyroplane" title="Breguet-Richet Gyroplane"><i>Gyroplane No.1</i></a>, possibly as the earliest known example of a quadcopter. Although there is some uncertainty about the date, sometime between 14 August and 29 September 1907, the Gyroplane No. 1 lifted its pilot into the air about two feet (0.6 m) for a minute.<sup id="cite_ref-Munson_6-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Munson-6">&#91;6&#93;</a></sup> The Gyroplane No. 1 proved to be extremely unsteady and required a man at each corner of the airframe to hold it steady. For this reason, the flights of the Gyroplane No. 1 are considered to be the first manned flight of a helicopter, but not a free or untethered flight.\n</p>\n<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:HE2G8.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fa/HE2G8.jpg/220px-HE2G8.jpg" width="220" height="69" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fa/HE2G8.jpg/330px-HE2G8.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fa/HE2G8.jpg/440px-HE2G8.jpg 2x" data-file-width="504" data-file-height="157" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:HE2G8.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Paul Cornu\'s helicopter, 1907</div></div></div>\n<p>That same year, fellow French inventor <a href="/wiki/Paul_Cornu" title="Paul Cornu">Paul Cornu</a> designed and built a <a href="/wiki/Cornu_helicopter" title="Cornu helicopter">Cornu helicopter</a> that used two 20-foot (6 m) counter-rotating rotors driven by a 24&#160;hp (18&#160;kW) <a href="/wiki/Antoinette_(manufacturer)" title="Antoinette (manufacturer)">Antoinette</a> engine. On 13 November 1907, it lifted its inventor to 1 foot (0.3 m) and remained aloft for 20 seconds. Even though this flight did not surpass the flight of the Gyroplane No. 1, it was reported to be the first truly free flight with a pilot.<sup id="cite_ref-23" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-23">&#91;n 1&#93;</a></sup> Cornu\'s helicopter completed a few more flights and achieved a height of nearly 6.5 feet (2 m), but it proved to be unstable and was abandoned.<sup id="cite_ref-Munson_6-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Munson-6">&#91;6&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>In 1911, Slovenian philosopher and economist Ivan Slokar patented a helicopter configuration.<sup id="cite_ref-24" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-24">&#91;23&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-25" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-25">&#91;24&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-26" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-26">&#91;25&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>The Danish inventor <a href="/wiki/Jacob_Ellehammer" title="Jacob Ellehammer">Jacob Ellehammer</a> built the <a href="/wiki/Ellehammer_helicopter" title="Ellehammer helicopter">Ellehammer helicopter</a> in 1912. It consisted of a frame equipped with two counter-rotating discs, each of which was fitted with six vanes around its circumference. After indoor tests, the aircraft was demonstrated outdoors and made several free take-offs. Experiments with the helicopter continued until September 1916, when it tipped over during take-off, destroying its rotors.<sup id="cite_ref-27" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-27">&#91;26&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>During <a href="/wiki/World_War_I" title="World War I">World War I</a>, <a href="/wiki/Austria-Hungary" title="Austria-Hungary">Austria-Hungary</a> developed the <a href="/wiki/Petr%C3%B3czy-K%C3%A1rm%C3%A1n-%C5%BDurovec" title="Petr\xc3\xb3czy-K\xc3\xa1rm\xc3\xa1n-\xc5\xbdurovec"> PKZ</a>, an experimental helicopter prototype, with two aircraft built.\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Early_development">Early development</span></h3>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><div id="mwe_player_0" class="PopUpMediaTransform" style="width:220px;" videopayload="&lt;div class=&quot;mediaContainer&quot;
